When McDonald's is bad, it's really bad, but when it's right there is nothing more right on this plane of existence. This particular franchise (the one on Grand Avenue in Arroyo Grande, CA) is consistently great. The food is always hot and fresh, and the service is friendly.

I'm lovin' it....<//Review>

< review>
I had my first massage since the pandemic started today with Amanda. Scheduling a few days beforehand was very easy. Before and during the session, Amanda was accommodating and communicative and helped me better understand my own massage preferences. Her space sets nice ambiance, and I walked out the most relaxed I've been in a long time.

Money very well spent, and I will certainly be back soon!<//review>

<Name>Evan Schwartz< /Name>< time>
1526101536065</time>
<Rate>4< /Rate><review>Clark Kerr is a beautiful place to live, and the commute, while far, is often exaggerated. There's lots of natural scenery, big rooms and lounges, and it's adjacent to student-accessible track, pool, tennis courts, volleyball pits, and hiking trails. And it is surrounded by a similarly beautiful neighborhood that makes you feel as though you are frequently separated from the chaos of the UC campus. This, however, comes with a downside of feeling isolated from the campus activity and prone to staying in your dorm room rather than getting out and involved at school.
All in all, the one serious downside to Clark Kerr is the uniquely antisocial atmosphere. Certain cliques -- primarily the athletes and the frat/sorority rushers -- dominate the dorms in a homogeneous and unaccepting way. It's difficult to avoid them, and it can get annoying if you do not fit nicely into them. There certainly aren't as many hardcore STEM kids here; it's generally more a party culture kind of group, if you're into that.
Living here for a third year now, so there is definitely a net benefit. But you need to be prepared for the kinds of exclusive crowds you encounter here. Of course, there will be decent kids, but it's definitely a different kind of group predominating here.<//review><pics>None<//pics>< Response>
None< /Response>

<user_id>103468007455237318699< /user_id><GmapID>0x80e914788d29a497:0x216c8d2c2b88a634</GmapID>< review>
I like this place. It's about as close to an East Coast/Rust Belt bar as you're going to find here in sunny Santa Barbara. It gets a little too crowded for me on weekend nights, but I'm not a kid anymore, so judge accordingly. It's got a British rock and roll theme, and it seems like there are actual British ex-pats that hang out there. I have often seen a few dogs in there, and they seem as well behaved as the regulars. No darts, but that's all that's missing. It's refreshingly not corporate, in a land filled with yet another Jimmy Buffett themed bar. I expect they would tell Guy Fieri to take a hike.<//review>

<gmap_id>0x80ece19c5043ae4b:0x5a21f380c8631f5f< /gmap_id>< review>
I don't write reviews, but I thought I would tell my cautionary tale. It was my first and last experience here.

Waitress served flat soda with no ice cubes. Didn't tell us that they were out of icecubes. They gave us water instead. Chocked it off.

I thought the chips and salsa they served were flat-tasting. Well, at least it was the "free" part of the meal. But I am starting to wonder.

Receive the small carne asada burrito, and my fiance got the cheese enchiladas. What we really got were soupy, cheese dishes. Mine had a little bit of carne asada, but there was cheese stuffed inside and then cheese melted on top. Both plates were floating in a soup of melted cheese, and greasy red sauce

Don't get me wrong. I love cheese, but when all you can taste is cheese, and after a couple hours you feel sick and bloated (from all that cheese). Well, that is unfortunate because the place came recommended.

Maybe your experience will be different. They seriously need to cut back the cheese, and might even save some money in the process.<//review>

< review>
I shop here quite often and spend a great deal of money every year.  Today's visit got me thinking it's time to shop somewhere else.

This year, I spent almost $400 on Christmas ornaments at CB (purchased during the end of October) and last night, I happened to notice all the items I purchased was on sale for 20% off.  So... I decided to stop by to request a price adjustment.

Instead of providing excellent customer service, the manager on duty made it seem as if he was doing me a favor by accommodating my request.  At first, he tried to deter me by telling me I was past the 2 week store policy for price matching but then I had to remind him that I was still within my 90 day refund policy and that I can easily return everything and then repurchase it back at the same price. After thinking this through, he then back peddled and became a bit more willing to assist.  Hmmmm... Not too bright, are we?

For sure I will be expanding my shopping to other comparable retailers like Pottery Barn and William Sonoma going forward.  Bye CB!</review>

Attorney Kelly O'Reilly was very helpful and showed much empathy without oversimplifying the problem.  Nor does he overpromise.  He lays down his assessment and readily provides his POV on how to approach the issue.  He dissects the problem and arrives at the solution based on his experience  working for the USCIS and deep knowledge of the US Immigration Law.

Jeannie Tsoi, Sonia Garibaldi, and Johanna  Felix, Attorney Kelly's associates, were also extremely helpful and accommodating.  They patiently answered my questions (both via email and phone conversations).
Very reassuring - as if I was working with my own family!  And of course  Tess  de Guzman in Reception was such an efficient, helpful, and empathetic presence in the law firm that all my nervousness and trepidation died down while waiting to be called in for my appointment.

Overall:  highly recommended.  Fees are reasonable and client servicing is very warm, efficient, and professional.< /review>
